Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
The Heart as the Seat of Faith: Maturidi's Refutation of Hypocrites
Maturidi argues that hypocrites are disbelievers and establishes the heart as the seat of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi classifies hypocrites as disbelievers and how he establishes the heart as the true locus of faith using Quranic proofs.

Core Idea
True faith is settled in the heart, not merely spoken on the tongue.

Maturidi confronts the claim that hypocrites have faith. He uses Quranic evidence to show that outward profession without inner affirmation (tasdiq) is a lie, and that the heart is the true seat of faith. This lesson examines his scriptural argument and linguistic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the repeated Quranic citations and the logical flow from God's information to the conclusion about the heart.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
List the verses Maturidi quotes. For each, ask: how does it support his claim that hypocrites are disbelievers?
Verses include: 'If they desist...' (8:38), 'And whoever does that...' (25:68-70), 'God bears witness...' (63:1), 'On the Day...' (63:1-2?), 'Do not make excuses...' (9:66), 'They will swear...' (63:2), 'The more honorable...' (63:8), 'Except one who is forced...' (16:106).
3
Understand the linguistic argument
Maturidi states that faith (iman) linguistically means tasdiq (affirmation by the heart). He argues that making the hypocrites' verbal profession 'faith' would be a contradiction, since their hearts deny.
This connects the definition of faith to inner conviction.
4
Recognize the verse on coercion (ikrah)
The verse 'Except one who is forced while his heart is settled in faith' shows that verbal disbelief is not counted when the heart affirms faith. This proves the heart is the seat of faith, not the tongue.
Maturidi uses this as a positive proof for the heart's role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك مما أخبر الله عن المنافقين أنهم كفروا ، والكفر ضد الإيمان ، وبالإيمان ننتهى عن الكفر . وقال الله تعالى : إِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ . وقال : تعالى : وَمَنْ يَفْعَلُ ذَلِكَ يَلْقَ آثَامًا إلى آخر تلك الآيات وإذ ثبت أن المنافقين كفرة في التحقيق ، كذبة في قولهم بما قال الله ، والله يشهد أن المنافقين لكاذبون . وقال : يَوْمَ يَبْعَثُهُم اللَّهُ جَمِيعًا ، أخبر أنهم كذبة ، فجعل قول الإسلام منهم على جحوده القلب كذبا ، فمن جعل ذلك إيمانا - والإيمان في اللغة التصديق فقد جعل الشيء ضده ، وذلك فاسد . وقال : لا تَعْتَذِرُوا قَدْ كَفَرْتُمْ بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ ، وقال : سَيَحْلِفُونَ بِاللَّهِ لَكُم إِذَا انْقَلَبْتُمْ إِلَيْهِمْ ، وقال : لَيُخْرِجَنَّ الْأَعَزُّ مِنْهَا الْأَزَلَ وَلِلَّهِ العِزَّةُ وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَلَكِنَّ المُنَافِقِينَ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ، أخبر أنهم كفرة، وأنهم لا يعلمون لمن العزة ، وأنها لمن ذكر ، ولو كانوا لكانت منهم لهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ما جعل الله ذلك منهم استهزاء ومخادعة وسخرية وأوجب لهم جزاء ذلك ، يكون الإيمان هذا وصفه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ولم يجز وقد قال الله : إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنُ بِالإِيمَانِ ، لم يجعل لهم كفر باللسان إذا لم يكن / عبارة عن القلب ، ذلك بايمان القلب ، فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان ، وبالله التوفيق .
That is part of what God informed about the hypocrites: that they disbelieved. And disbelief is the opposite of faith, and by faith we are prohibited from disbelief. And God Most High said: 'If they desist, what is past will be forgiven them.' And He said: 'And whoever does that will meet penalty.' ... And when it is established that the hypocrites are, in reality, disbelievers, liars in what they say, as God said: 'And God bears witness that the hypocrites are liars.' And He said: 'On the Day when God raises them all together' — He informed that they are liars. So He made their utterance of Islam accompanied by the denial of the heart a lie. So whoever makes that faith — while faith in language is tasdiq (affirmation) — has made a thing its opposite, and that is corrupt. And He said: 'Do not make excuses; you have disbelieved after your faith.' And He said: 'They will swear by God to you when you return to them.' And He said: 'The more honorable [party] will surely expel from it the more abased. And to God belongs honor, and to His Messenger, and to the believers, but the hypocrites do not know.' He informed that they are disbelievers, and that they do not know to whom honor belongs, and that it belongs to those mentioned. And if they were [believers], it would have been from them for them. There is no power except with God. God made that from them mockery, deceit, and ridicule, and He obligated for them the recompense for that. Can faith be described in this manner? There is no power except with God. And He did not deem it permissible — while God said: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is settled in faith' — He did not make for them disbelief with the tongue if it is not an expression of the heart; that is due to faith of the heart. So it is established that the heart is the place of faith. And with God is assistance.
Source pages p. 974

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the hypocrites' claim to faith. Maturidi begins by citing God's information that hypocrites disbelieve, noting that disbelief is the opposite of faith. He then quotes several Quranic verses to demonstrate that hypocrites are, in reality, disbelievers despite their verbal profession. Their verbal Islam is a lie because their hearts deny. Since faith linguistically means tasdiq (affirmation), making their verbal profession faith would be contradictory. He addresses the verse about coercion (ikrah): God does not count verbal disbelief when the heart is settled in faith, because the heart is the seat. Thus the conclusion: the heart is the locus of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان (faith)
كفر (disbelief)
نفاق (hypocrisy)
تصديق (affirmation)
قلب (heart)
إكراه (coercion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That outwardly professing Islam, even with a denying heart, is sufficient for faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that hypocrites are disbelievers because their hearts deny, and that faith (iman) linguistically requires inner tasdiq. The verse on coercion (16:106) proves that the heart is the true locus of faith.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi in this passage, what is the linguistic meaning of faith (iman)?
A) Confession by the tongue
B) Affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart
C) Actions of the limbs
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Faith is true only when the heart affirms; the tongue's confession without inner conviction is hypocrisy and disbelief, as proven by Quranic verses and the linguistic meaning of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'La ilaha illa Allah' with your tongue, is there any area of your life where your heart secretly denies His sovereignty? What would it take to bring that area into submission?
?
The hypocrites are called liars because their hearts contradict their words. Have you ever performed an act of worship while your heart was absorbed in something displeasing to Allah? How will you guard against that gap?
?
If you were seized and forced to utter words of disbelief, would your heart remain settled in faith as described in verse 16:106? What are you doing today to strengthen that inner certainty?

Faith and Disbelief

Outward Declaration as a Sign of Faith in Worldly Judgments
Maturidi establishes that verbal profession is a sign and expression of faith, accepted in apparent rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Maturidi considers outward verbal profession as a sign (dalil) and expression ('ibara) of inner faith, and why it is accepted in worldly judgments despite our inability to know the heart.

Core Idea
Your tongue is the witness of your heart in this world, but not the final judge.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a crucial question: If we cannot see into people's hearts, how do we judge their faith in worldly affairs? He explains that the verbal declaration of faith is a sign and expression, and it is on this basis that we accept it in legal and social matters. This lesson unpacks that foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp Maturidi's statement.
Pay attention to the terms دليل and عبارة.
2
Identify the key terms
Note the terms دليل (evidence) and عبارة (expression) and see how they function in the argument.
3
Understand the principle
Maturidi states that we accept the outward expression because we have no access to the inner reality.
This is the core of the lesson.
4
Connect to general practice
He says this applies to most matters among people, not just faith.
5
Reflect on the limit
The acceptance is for this world; it does not guarantee the hereafter.
This connects to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس بما يقاتلون إلى أن يشهدوا باللسان دليل أن ذلك هو الإيمان أو لا إيمان بالقلوب ، بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه ، فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم يه، وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها ما كان فى الذى بيتنا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفر [ق] وبين المؤمنين بالإعلام وأنواع .... أو المخالطة مع الأهل وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام ، إفمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بينا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص ، فمثله الذي نحن فيه ، والله أعلم . إنما يعير : وعلى ذلك أمر المكرة على الكفر ، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عما في قلبه لسانه ، وعلى ما ذكرت أمر الأملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علمه ذلك الأمور الظاهرة ، علمه ذلك الأمور الظاهرة ، فمثله حكم القبول ، وقد تجد الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله ، وفى ذلك الترك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها ، وإن كان لا يحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان ويحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الدين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم الأحكام ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم يقال لهم : فإن كان ما يقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلا على أنه خاصة فلما حرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم ۱۱۰] والثواب / الجزيل . ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة فى الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And it is not that they fight until they testify with the tongue as evidence that this is faith or that there is no faith in hearts. Rather, that from them is a evidence (dalil) of faith and an expression ('ibara) thereof, so their statement is accepted in apparent rulings by virtue of the expression regarding that for which we have no way to know the actual reality. And upon that are general matters among people, carried upon what their capacity of knowledge can bear, even if they have other realities that do not have in what we have of evidence indicating that. Similarly, the inherited practice in distinguishing between disbelief [q] and believers by information and types ... or mixing with the family, even if that is not disbelief or Islam, so likewise is the matter of expression with the tongue. And upon this is what we have clarified of verses regarding knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts according to what came in texts, so its likeness is what we are in. And God knows best. ... And upon that is the matter of the one coerced into disbelief, and the statement of the Prophet of God, peace be upon him, that 'what is in his heart is [expressed by] his tongue,' and upon what I mentioned of the matter of testimonies and oaths and types of schools in religions, by which He knows apparent matters, so its likeness is the ruling of acceptance. And you find that God commanded to fight so they pay jizya and to grant asylum until they hear the words of God, and in that is the interaction among Muslims to live together to examine their affairs and reflect on their rulings so they know thereby their realities, even if it is not possible to base it on what is in it of reconciliation of hearts and prevention of injustice and types of corruption except by God, so that their hearts become reassured with faith and their souls deem it possible to respond to Islam. So likewise in religion: they manifested faith in God and responded to the believers regarding what they have of rulings. There is no power except with God. Then it is said to them: If what is accepted from them of faith in the apparent rulings by the tongue is evidence that it is specifically [faith], then why are they deprived of forgiveness and the promised eternal bliss and abundant reward? And then by what does not permit them to worship in reality and they do not attain virtue from God — evidence that they are not believers. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage discusses the role of outward declaration. Maturidi states that verbal testimony is a sign (dalil) and expression ('ibara) of inner faith. In worldly judgments, we accept the verbal profession even though we cannot know the heart. This is the principle in most human dealings. He then refers to the inherited practice of distinguishing believers from disbelievers by outward signs. He addresses the case of coercion (ikrah): the Prophet's statement indicates that the tongue reveals the heart. He also mentions that God commands fighting to enforce jizya and to grant asylum, which are based on apparent submission. The ultimate point: if the verbal declaration alone were sufficient for true faith, then hypocrites would deserve the rewards of faith, but they are denied that. Thus, true faith requires inner belief.

Key Terms
دليل (evidence)
عبارة (expression)
ظواهر الأحكام (apparent rulings)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Acceptance of verbal profession in worldly matters implies salvation in the hereafter.
Correction: Maturidi explains that verbal profession is only a sign and expression, not the reality of faith; acceptance is limited to worldly judgments.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the basis for accepting verbal declaration in worldly rulings?
A) It is identical to inner faith
B) It is a sign and expression of faith
C) It is required by law
D) It is forced

Key Takeaway
In worldly judgments, a person's verbal profession of faith is accepted as a sign of their inner state, even though the ultimate reality of their faith is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you utter the shahada, do you ever pause to ask yourself whether your tongue is merely performing a ritual while your heart remains distant? What concrete step can you take today to bridge that gap between your outward profession and your inner conviction?
?
This lesson teaches that we accept others' verbal profession as a sign of faith in worldly dealings, even though we cannot know their hearts. How does this challenge your own tendency to judge someone's faith by their actions or words alone? Will you now treat others with more caution in your judgments, remembering that only Allah knows what is truly in their hearts?
?
If you knew that your verbal profession is enough for people to consider you a believer, would that settle your conscience? Or does the thought that Allah sees your heart make you uneasy? What specific change in your daily life would demonstrate that you truly care about what is hidden as much as what is apparent?

The Hypocrite's Dilemma: Outward Profession Does Not Guarantee Salvation
Maturidi argues that hypocrites' exclusion from eternal rewards proves that verbal profession alone is not true faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that if outward profession alone were sufficient for true faith, then hypocrites would deserve the rewards of the hereafter, which they do not; thus, true faith requires inner conviction.

Core Idea
Words alone cannot buy paradise; the hypocrite's tongue testifies but the heart denies.

Having established that verbal declaration is accepted in worldly matters, Maturidi now turns to a critical objection: If we accept the hypocrite's words here, does that mean they are truly believers? He answers with a clear argument that outward acceptance does not entitle them to the rewards of true faith. This lesson examines that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the final part from 'ثم يقال لهم' to the end.
Note the rhetorical question format.
2
Understand the scenario
Maturidi imagines an objection: if verbal profession is enough for faith, why are hypocrites deprived of rewards?
3
Analyze the response
He argues that since they are denied forgiveness and paradise, their profession cannot be true faith.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Worldly judgments accept the outward, but divine judgment is based on the inner reality.
This reinforces the lesson's core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is not that they fight until they testify with the tongue as evidence that this is faith or that there is no faith in hearts. Rather, that from them is a evidence (dalil) of faith and an expression ('ibara) thereof, so their statement is accepted in apparent rulings by virtue of the expression regarding that for which we have no way to know the actual reality. And upon that are general matters among people, carried upon what their capacity of knowledge can bear, even if they have other realities that do not have in what we have of evidence indicating that. Commentary
This passage discusses the role of outward declaration. Maturidi states that verbal testimony is a sign (dalil) and expression ('ibara) of inner faith. Thus, true faith requires inner belief.

Key Terms
غفران (forgiveness)
نعيم (bliss)
ثواب (reward)
مؤمن (believer)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Outward profession of faith guarantees salvation and eternal reward.
Correction: Maturidi argues that hypocrites who only profess with the tongue are deprived of forgiveness and reward, proving that true faith requires inner belief.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to argue that the hypocrite's verbal profession is not true faith?
A) They pay jizya
B) They are deprived of forgiveness and eternal reward
C) They are coerced
D) They mix with believers

Key Takeaway
The hypocrite's exclusion from eternal rewards demonstrates that verbal profession alone is insufficient for true faith; inner conviction is essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe,' do you ever stop to consider that your tongue may be ahead of your heart? What would it take for you to close that gap today?
?
If your outward profession were all that mattered, would your heart be content with that? Or does the thought that God knows what is in your heart make you uneasy?
?
The hypocrite's worship is not accepted because of their inner denial. Is there any area of your life where your outward actions contradict your inner state? What will you do about it now?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Principle of Accepting Verbal Declaration
Maturidi states the principle of accepting verbal testimony due to inaccessible inward reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi insists that verbal testimony of faith is accepted only in outward rulings, not as proof of inner faith.

Core Idea
Outward rulings rely on apparent declarations; true faith is hidden in the heart.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing a fundamental principle: when someone verbally declares faith, we accept it for legal purposes because we cannot know what is in their heart. This does not mean that verbal declaration is the reality of faith. In this lesson, you will examine his initial argument and the reasoning behind this critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Maturidi distinguishes between outward testimony and inward reality.
The passage is dense; focus on the key phrase 'بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به'
2
Identify the core claim
Identify Maturidi's main claim: verbal testimony is an expression (عبارة) of faith, not faith itself, and is accepted only because we have no access to the heart.
3
Understand the generalization
Maturidi extends this principle to all human affairs: judgments are based on appearances. Note his phrase 'عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم'
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: How does this principle affect how we treat others? Does it mean we never judge inner faith?
Maturidi is not denying that some people have true faith; he is only saying we cannot verify it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس بما يقاتلون إلى أن يشهدوا باللسان دليل أن ذلك هو الإيمان أو لا إيمان بالقلوب، بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه، فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به، وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها ما كان في الذي بينا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفر [ق] وبين المؤمنين بالإعلام وأنواع ... أو المخالطة مع الأهل وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام، فمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بينا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص، فمثله الذي نحن فيه، والله أعلم. وعلى ذلك أمر المكرة على الكفر، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عما في قلبه لسانه، وعلى ما ذكرت أمر الأملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علمه ذلك الأمور الظاهرة، فمثله حكم القبول، وقد تجد الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله، وفي ذلك الترك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها، وإن كان لا يحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان ويحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الدين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم الأحكام، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم يقال لهم: فإن كان ما يقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلا على أنه خاصة فلما حرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب الجزيل. ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين، ولا قوة إلا بالله. يقال: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار، قال الله عز وجل: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار، وقاتلوا المشركين كافة، وقال: فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم، على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم يجب بهذا أن يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب، فما يبعد أن يؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا ثم يمنع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع إيمان القلب؛ إذ هذا كونه فيه، والله الموفق. ثم يقال لهم: في الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله، حتى يشهدوا، فيكون الشهادتين سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
It is not that they fight until they testify with the tongue is evidence that that is faith or no faith in hearts, rather that is from them evidence of faith and expression of it, so their statement is accepted in outward rulings by right of expression since we have no way to the reality of knowledge of it. And upon that are all matters among creatures carried on what is within their capacity of knowledge, even if they have realities other than that which was in what we explained as indication of that. And likewise the inherited matter in distinguishing between disbelief [q] and between believers by information and types... or association with family even if that is not disbelief nor Islam, so the matter of expression by the tongue is similar. And upon this are what we explained of the verses regarding knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts in what the texts brought, so similar is that which we are in, and God knows best. And upon that is the matter of those compelled to disbelief, and the saying of the Prophet of God, peace be upon him, about what is in his heart his tongue, and upon what I mentioned is the matter of angels and testimonies and types of sects in religions by what is known of outward matters, so similar is the ruling of acceptance. And you may find that God commanded to fight to give the jizya and to be given asylum until they hear the word of God, and in that is the leaving among Muslims to live to look into their affairs and reflect on their rulings so that they may know thereby their realities, even if it is not possible to establish them on what is in them of bringing hearts together and repelling injustice and types of corruption except by God to reassure their hearts with faith and to incline their souls to respond to Islam, so similar is it in religion that they manifested faith in God and responded to the believers with what they have of rulings, and there is no power except with God. Then it is said to them: If what is accepted from them of faith in the outward aspects of rulings by the tongue is evidence that it is the special characteristic, then why were they deprived by it of forgiveness and the promised reward on faith of eternal bliss and great recompense. Then by what is not permitted for them in reality of worship nor do they attain by it virtue before God is evidence that they are not believers, and there is no power except with God. It is said: Fight those who are near you of the disbelievers, God Almighty said: Fight those who are near you of the disbelievers, and fight the polytheists all together, and He said: Then kill the polytheists wherever you find them, based on what they manifest of polytheism and disbelief not what they conceal, and it is not necessary by this that polytheism and disbelief are in hearts. So how far is it that one is commanded to fight until they believe then prohibited from fighting if they manifest faith by the tongue even if the reality is the place of heart’s faith? For this is its being in it, and God is the giver of success. Then it is said to them: In the report, I was commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but God, until they testify, so the two testimonies are cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument in which Imam Maturidi defends the distinction between the outward acceptance of verbal testimony in worldly rulings and the inward reality of faith in the heart. He begins by stating that those who fight and then verbally declare faith are not necessarily revealing true inner faith; rather, their tongue is evidence of faith and an expression of it, and we accept their statement for outward rulings because we have no access to the hidden reality. This principle applies to many interpersonal matters where judgments are based on apparent indications. He then cites the inherited practice of distinguishing between believers and disbelievers based on outward declarations and interactions. The argument is supported by the prophetic statement that the tongue reveals what is in the heart, and by Quranic commands to fight polytheists based on their outward manifestation of disbelief, not their inner state. He addresses an objection: if verbal declaration were the special reality of faith, then why do those who merely declare with the tongue not receive the full reward of faith? He answers that such people are not considered true believers in the sight of God, because they lack inner conviction. He then cites the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' and concludes that the declaration is only a cause for sparing life, not a proof of true faith. Throughout, he maintains that outward rulings are based on apparent actions, while the reality of faith remains with God.

Key Terms
إيمان
لسان
قلب
أحكام ظاهرة
عبارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that when someone declares faith with the tongue, they are definitely a true believer in the sight of God.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that verbal declaration is only an expression accepted for worldly rulings; the reality of faith remains hidden in the heart and known only to God.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is verbal testimony of faith accepted in outward rulings?
A) It always reflects true inner faith
B) We have no way to know the reality of the heart
C) The Prophet commanded acceptance without exception
D) It is equivalent to faith in the heart

Key Takeaway
Verbal declaration of faith is accepted for outward rulings because we cannot know the heart, but it does not confirm true faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you judge others based on their outward declarations while ignoring your own hidden hypocrisy? What would you do today if someone you consider a hypocrite gave you sincere advice? Would you accept it because of the outward statement, or dismiss it because of your assumption about their heart?
?
Have you ever been tempted to pretend to believe something you don't, knowing that people will accept your outward statement? This lesson says that such acceptance is only for outward rulings—but what about your standing before Allah? What specific step will you take to ensure your tongue and heart are aligned, starting with one area where you know they are not?
?
You cannot know anyone's inner faith, including your own spouse or closest friend. How does that change the way you interact with them when they make a mistake that could be interpreted as disbelief? Will you demand an explanation that satisfies your curiosity, or will you accept their outward repentance and leave their innermost state to Allah? Which is harder for you, and why?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and Practice
Maturidi cites prophetic hadith and Quranic verses to support outward acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic commands, prophetic hadith, and practical examples to support the principle of accepting outward declarations.

Core Idea
Quran and Sunnah command action based on outward manifestation, not inner states.

Maturidi strengthens his argument by referencing key evidences: the Prophet's saying that the tongue reveals the heart, Quranic commands to fight polytheists based on their outward disbelief, and the practice of accepting jizya based on outward submission. In this lesson, you will explore these proofs and see how they align with the principle that outward rulings depend on external expressions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage of evidences
Read the second part of the source, which begins with 'وعلى ذلك أمر المكرة...'. Identify each piece of evidence Maturidi cites.
Look for the hadith about the tongue revealing the heart and the Quranic verses about fighting polytheists.
2
Analyze the prophetic hadith
Maturidi cites the Prophet's statement about the tongue revealing what is in the heart. Consider how this supports the principle of accepting verbal testimony.
The hadith is not quoted word-for-word but referenced.
3
Examine the Quranic commands
Maturidi quotes verses commanding to fight polytheists based on what they manifest. Notice the contrast: we fight based on outward polytheism, but we stop when they outwardly declare faith, even if their hearts are not convinced.
The key verse is 'قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار' and 'فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم'
4
Consider the practical implications
Maturidi mentions the practice of jizya and asylum to hear God's word. How does this show that outward acceptance is sufficient for worldly dealings?

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument in which Imam Maturidi defends the distinction between the outward acceptance of verbal testimony in worldly rulings and the inward reality of faith in the heart. He begins by stating that those who fight and then verbally declare faith are not necessarily revealing true inner faith; rather, their tongue is evidence of faith and an expression of it, and we accept their statement for outward rulings because we have no access to the hidden reality. This principle applies to many interpersonal matters where judgments are based on apparent indications. He then cites the inherited practice of distinguishing between believers and disbelievers based on outward declarations and interactions. The argument is supported by the prophetic statement that the tongue reveals what is in the heart, and by Quranic commands to fight polytheists based on their outward manifestation of disbelief, not their inner state. He addresses an objection: if verbal declaration were the special reality of faith, then why do those who merely declare with the tongue not receive the full reward of faith? He answers that such people are not considered true believers in the sight of God, because they lack inner conviction. He then cites the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' and concludes that the declaration is only a cause for sparing life, not a proof of true faith. Throughout, he maintains that outward rulings are based on apparent actions, while the reality of faith remains with God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that your tongue can declare faith while your heart is distant. If your life depended on outward conformity alone, would you be satisfied with that as your state before Allah? What one concrete step will you take this week to bring your heart closer to what your tongue professes?
?
Think of a person you have judged negatively based on their outward actions. Did you assume you knew their inner state? How does this lesson's insistence on judging only by outward manifestation challenge your tendency to condemn others? What would it change if you stopped presuming intentions?
?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Objection and Final Clarification on Verbal Testimony
Maturidi refutes objection and interprets the hadith as cause for sparing life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the objection that verbal declaration might be the reality of faith, and why the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' is interpreted as a cause for sparing life, not as proof of faith.

Core Idea
Verbal declaration is a legal cause, not the reality of faith.

In this final lesson, Maturidi addresses a potential objection: if verbal declaration were the essence of faith, why do those who only say the words not receive the full reward? He answers by explaining that such people are not true believers. He then interprets the famous hadith about fighting until people say 'la ilaha illallah' as a ruling for worldly life protection, not a definition of faith. This lesson solidifies the distinction between outward acceptance and inner reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the final part starting with 'ثم يقال لهم...'. Identify the objection and Maturidi's response.
The objection is: if verbal declaration is the special characteristic of faith, why don't those who merely declare get rewards?
2
Analyze the response
Maturidi responds by saying that those who only declare with the tongue are not true believers because they lack inner faith and cannot attain true worship or virtue.
He says: 'بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة'
3
Examine the hadith interpretation
Maturidi cites the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' and explains that the testimony is a cause (سبب) for preventing killing, not the reality of faith.
The key phrase: 'سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان'
4
Connect to Quranic commands
He also revisits the Quranic command to fight polytheists based on outward manifestation, showing consistency: we fight based on outward disbelief, and we stop based on outward faith.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Reflect on how all three lessons together show that in Islam, worldly rulings are based on apparent actions, while the true state of faith is known only to God.

وليس بما يقاتلون إلى أن يشهدوا باللسان دليل أن ذلك هو الإيمان أو لا إيمان بالقلوب، بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه، فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به، وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها ما كان في الذي بينا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفر [ق] وبين المؤمنين بالإعلام وأنواع ... أو المخالطة مع الأهل وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام، فمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بينا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص، فمثله الذي نحن فيه، والله أعلم. وعلى ذلك أمر المكرة على الكفر، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عما في قلبه لسانه، وعلى ما ذكرت أمر الأملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علمه ذلك الأمور الظاهرة، فمثله حكم القبول، وقد تجد الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله، وفي ذلك الترك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها، وإن كان لا يحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان ويحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الدين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم الأحكام، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم يقال لهم: فإن كان ما يقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلا على أنه خاصة فلما حرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب الجزيل. ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين، ولا قوة إلا بالله. يقال: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار، قال الله عز وجل: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار، وقاتلوا المشركين كافة، وقال: فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم، على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم يجب بهذا أن يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب، فما يبعد أن يؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا ثم يمنع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع إيمان القلب؛ إذ هذا كونه فيه، والله الموفق. ثم يقال لهم: في الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله، حتى يشهدوا، فيكون الشهادتين سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
It is not that they fight until they testify with the tongue is evidence that that is faith or no faith in hearts, rather that is from them evidence of faith and expression of it, so their statement is accepted in outward rulings by right of expression since we have no way to the reality of knowledge of it. And upon that are all matters among creatures carried on what is within their capacity of knowledge, even if they have realities other than that which was in what we explained as indication of that. And likewise the inherited matter in distinguishing between disbelief [q] and between believers by information and types... or association with family even if that is not disbelief nor Islam, so the matter of expression by the tongue is similar. And upon this are what we explained of the verses regarding knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts in what the texts brought, so similar is that which we are in, and God knows best. And upon that is the matter of those compelled to disbelief, and the saying of the Prophet of God, peace be upon him, about what is in his heart his tongue, and upon what I mentioned is the matter of angels and testimonies and types of sects in religions by what is known of outward matters, so similar is the ruling of acceptance. And you may find that God commanded to fight to give the jizya and to be given asylum until they hear the word of God, and in that is the leaving among Muslims to live to look into their affairs and reflect on their rulings so that they may know thereby their realities, even if it is not possible to establish them on what is in them of bringing hearts together and repelling injustice and types of corruption except by God to reassure their hearts with faith and to incline their souls to respond to Islam, so similar is it in religion that they manifested faith in God and responded to the believers with what they have of rulings, and there is no power except with God. Then it is said to them: If what is accepted from them of faith in the outward aspects of rulings by the tongue is evidence that it is the special characteristic, then why were they deprived by it of forgiveness and the promised reward on faith of eternal bliss and great recompense. Then by what is not permitted for them in reality of worship nor do they attain by it virtue before God is evidence that they are not believers, and there is no power except with God. It is said: Fight those who are near you of the disbelievers, God Almighty said: Fight those who are near you of the disbelievers, and fight the polytheists all together, and He said: Then kill the polytheists wherever you find them, based on what they manifest of polytheism and disbelief not what they conceal, and it is not necessary by this that polytheism and disbelief are in hearts. So how far is it that one is commanded to fight until they believe then prohibited from fighting if they manifest faith by the tongue even if the reality is the place of heart’s faith? For this is its being in it, and God is the giver of success. Then it is said to them: In the report, I was commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but God, until they testify, so the two testimonies are cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument in which Imam Maturidi defends the distinction between the outward acceptance of verbal testimony in worldly rulings and the inward reality of faith in the heart. He begins by stating that those who fight and then verbally declare faith are not necessarily revealing true inner faith; rather, their tongue is evidence of faith and an expression of it, and we accept their statement for outward rulings because we have no access to the hidden reality. This principle applies to many interpersonal matters where judgments are based on apparent indications. He then cites the inherited practice of distinguishing between believers and disbelievers based on outward declarations and interactions. The argument is supported by the prophetic statement that the tongue reveals what is in the heart, and by Quranic commands to fight polytheists based on their outward manifestation of disbelief, not their inner state. He addresses an objection: if verbal declaration were the special reality of faith, then why do those who merely declare with the tongue not receive the full reward of faith? He answers that such people are not considered true believers in the sight of God, because they lack inner conviction. He then cites the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' and concludes that the declaration is only a cause for sparing life, not a proof of true faith. Throughout, he maintains that outward rulings are based on apparent actions, while the reality of faith remains with God.

شهادة

Misconception: Some think that the hadith 'fight until they say la ilaha illallah' means that saying it makes one a true believer.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that it is only a legal cause to stop fighting, not an indication of inner faith.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the hadith 'I was commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illallah' indicate?
A) Saying the shahada guarantees salvation
B) The shahada is the reality of faith
C) The shahada is a cause to prevent killing, not the reality of faith
D) Fighting must continue until everyone believes

Key Takeaway
The shahada is a legal cause for worldly protection, not proof of inner faith; true faith is known only to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have recited the shahada countless times. But when you say it, do you consider that it may only be a legal protection for you in this world, while your heart remains distant from its true meaning? What would it take for your tongue and heart to be in complete agreement? Commit to a specific daily practice this week that aligns the two.
?
The lesson teaches that outward testimony spares life in this world but does not guarantee eternal reward. Are you secretly relying on your outward acts of worship—prayer, fasting, charity—to save you in the Hereafter, while neglecting the state of your heart? What hidden hypocrisy or spiritual complacency do you need to confess and correct today? Write it down and take one concrete step toward sincerity.
?
Maturidi argues that commands to fight are based on outward actions, not inner states. How often do you judge your fellow Muslims based on their outward appearance of faith—their beard, hijab, or public piety—assuming you know their inner reality? How does this passage challenge you to leave judgment to God and focus on your own heart's purification? What habit of judging others will you consciously break starting now?

Faith is an Act of the Heart, Not the Tongue
Maturidi refutes the Karramiyya by arguing faith is an act of the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that faith (iman) is primarily an act of the heart and not mere verbal confession, based on the Quranic principle that religion cannot be compelled.

Core Idea
Faith is what the heart embraces, not what the tongue merely pronounces.

This passage from Imam Maturidi is a key argument against those who reduce faith to verbal declaration. Maturidi points to the Quranic verse 'There is no compulsion in religion' to show that if faith were only speech, it could be forced—but God has negated compulsion, so faith must be an inward conviction of the heart. Through this and other evidence, he establishes the internal nature of iman.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Karrami position
The Karramiyya believed faith is in the heart but emphasized verbal confession. Notice how Maturidi uses their own premise against them.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's own flow come through.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses cited.
3
Analyze the key Quranic evidence
Identify the two Quranic verses Maturidi uses: 'There is no compulsion in religion' and 'Whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God'. How does each support his argument?
The no-compulsion verse is central.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters: if faith were only verbal, it could be faked or forced. Maturidi's argument protects the sincerity of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما ظنت الكرامية على أن الله تعالى أعلا درجة الإيمان في القلوب حتى أعلا الدرجات، وصير الإيمان مما يقوم به الخيرات، وعند وجوده تصل العبادات، وما يحتمل ما وصفت إنما هو القلوب لا الألسن؛ لذلك كانت أحق. وبعد، فإن الخطاب بالإيمان يلزم بالعقول، ويعرف حقيقة ما به الإيمان بالفكر والنظر، وذلك عمل القلوب، فمثل ذلك الإيمان. مع ما كان الألسن قد تستعمل وتخبر كغيرها الآيات، والله تعالى يقول: (لَا إِكْرَاهَ فِي الدِّينِ) لم يجز أن يجعل حقيقته فيما فيه الإكراه. وقال الله تعالى: (فَمَنْ يَكْفُرُ بِالطَّاغُوتِ وَيُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ) وليس الكفر بالطاغوت باللسان خاصة، فمثل ذلك الإيمان. ألا ترى إلى قوله: (أَلَمْ تَرَ إِلَى الَّذِينَ يَزْعُمُونَ) إلى قوله: (وَقَدْ أُمِرُوا أَنْ يَكْفُرُوا) فيصير الميل والتحاكم تركا للكفر وإن أخبر عن أنه مؤمن لسانه أنه يزعم به من بالذي عليه الإيمان به، والله الموفق.
The Karramiyya thought that God made the degree of faith in the hearts the highest of degrees, and made faith a means by which good deeds are performed, and at its presence acts of worship are valid. But what fits the description I have given is only the hearts, not the tongues; therefore they are more deserving. Moreover, the address concerning faith is obligated by intellects, and the reality of what faith is is known through reflection and consideration, and that is the work of the hearts. So such is faith. Even though the tongues may be used and inform like other instruments, but God says: 'There is no compulsion in religion' – it is not permissible to make its reality reside in something that involves compulsion. And God says: 'Whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God' – and disbelief in taghut is not solely by the tongue, so such is faith. Do you not see His saying: 'Have you not seen those who claim' up to His saying: 'and they were commanded to disbelieve' – so inclination and arbitration becomes an abandonment of disbelief, even if the tongue reports that he is a believer, because he claims to be with what faith is upon? And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 977

Commentary
This passage is a proof that faith (iman) is primarily an act of the heart, not the tongue. Maturidi begins by noting that the Karramiyya sect believed God placed faith in the heart, but they contradict that by emphasizing verbal confession. He argues that the very address of faith is directed to the intellect, and its reality is grasped through reflection, which is the work of the heart. To reinforce this, he cites the Quranic verse 'There is no compulsion in religion' (2:256): if faith were merely a verbal act, it could be forced, but compulsion is negated, so faith must be inward. He also cites the latter part of the same verse, 'Whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God', noting that disbelief in taghut is not solely by the tongue, so similarly faith must be more than speech. He further references the verse about those who claim to believe but are commanded to disbelieve (4:60), concluding that even if the tongue professes faith, the true state of belief or disbelief is in the heart. The passage refutes the Karramiyya and establishes the internal nature of iman.

Key Terms
الإيمان
القلب
اللسان
الكرامية
لا إكراه في الدين
الكفر بالطاغوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is only verbal confession.
Correction: Faith is primarily an inward conviction of the heart, proven by the negation of compulsion and other Quranic evidence.

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse does Maturidi use to argue that faith cannot be compelled?
A) (فَمَنْ يَكْفُرُ بِالطَّاغُوتِ وَيُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ)
B) (لَا إِكْرَاهَ فِي الدِّينِ)
C) (أَلَمْ تَرَ إِلَى الَّذِينَ يَزْعُمُونَ)
D) (وَقَدْ أُمِرُوا أَنْ يَكْفُرُوا)

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates through Quranic evidence that true faith is an internal act of the heart, not an external verbal declaration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada with your tongue, does your heart affirm it with full certainty? What is one area where your heart's conviction does not match your words, and what step will you take today to align them?
?
The passage says faith is known through reflection and consideration. When did you last deliberately reflect on the reality of your iman? Are you willing to set aside ten minutes tonight to honestly evaluate whether your faith is in your heart or just on your tongue?
?
If your faith were to be tested by compulsion tomorrow, would your inner conviction hold? What does your answer reveal about the depth of your iman, and what will you do this week to strengthen your heart's connection to Allah?

Faith and Disbelief

The Quranic Address 'O You Who Believe' Proves Faith is in the Heart
Maturidi argues that the Quranic address to believers even when they are silent proves iman is in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic address 'O you who believe' demonstrates that faith is fundamentally a state of the heart, not merely a verbal utterance.

Core Idea
Faith is a permanent reality in the heart, proven by God's address to believers even in silence.

Imam Maturidi draws a powerful argument directly from the Quran. When Allah addresses believers with 'O you who believe', He does so even when they are not speaking. This forces us to ask: what is the basis of that title? Maturidi's answer establishes that faith must be an inner reality, not just outward speech. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the key observation
Maturidi observes that the Quran repeatedly addresses believers as 'O you who believe'. No Muslim doubts that this address includes them.
3
Analyze the logical premise
The address applies even when believers are not using their tongues to speak words of faith. This is a crucial premise.
Think about times when a believer might be silent but still considered a believer.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the title 'believer' applies at all times, the reality that earns that name must be constantly present. That reality can only reside in the heart.
Thus, faith is not merely verbal but an inner state.
5
Reflect on the closing phrase
The passage ends with 'لا قوة إلا بالله', reminding us that all conclusion depend on God's grace.
This shows Maturidi's humility and reliance on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كتاب الله الخطاب بقوله: (يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا) في غير موضع، ثم لم يرتب أحد ممن ينسب إلى الإسلام والإيمان في ذلك أنه مما تضمنه، وإن لم يكن هو وقت فراغ الخطاب معه يستعمل لسانه في فعل الإيمان، ثبت أن حقيقته التي بها سماهم بهذا قائمة فيهم وقت الخطاب، وهى لا تحتمل إلا أن تكون في القلب، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And in the Book of God, the address by His saying: 'O you who have believed' in more than one place, and no one who traces himself to Islam and faith has doubted that this address includes them, even if at the time of the address he was not using his tongue in the act of faith; so it is established that its reality by which they are named with this name is present in them at the time of the address, and that cannot be except in the heart. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 977

Commentary
This passage is a proof based on the Quranic address 'O you who believe' (يا أيها الذين آمنوا). Maturidi observes that this address appears repeatedly in the Quran, and no Muslim doubts that it includes those who claim faith. However, at the moment the verse was revealed, many of the addressees were not actively using their tongues to express faith (e.g., they were silent or engaged in other acts). Yet they are still called 'believers'. Therefore, the reality that earns them that name must be something permanently present in them at all times, not just during speech. The only possible location for this permanent reality is the heart. Thus, faith is fundamentally an inner state, not an outward verbal act. The phrase 'لا قوة إلا بالله' is a closing invocation of reliance on God.

Key Terms
الإيمان
القلب
الخطاب
يا أيها الذين آمنوا
استعمال اللسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quranic address 'O you who believe' only applies to those actively speaking or declaring faith with the tongue.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the address includes believers even when they are silent, so faith must be a permanent inner reality in the heart, not dependent on outward speech.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say the Quranic address 'يا أيها الذين آمنوا' proves faith is in the heart?
A) Because the address is only for those who believe with the tongue.
B) Because believers are addressed even when not speaking, so faith must be a permanent state in the heart.
C) Because the address was revealed only at the moment of conversion.
D) Because the address requires an outward declaration.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic address 'O you who believe' proves that faith is an inner state of the heart, not dependent on outward speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are personally addressed as 'O you who believe' every time you recite or hear the Qur'an. Does your heart truly acknowledge that you are a believer, or do you sometimes feel like an imposter? What would change if you lived with the certainty that God sees your heart as a place of iman?
?
The passage says faith is in your heart even when you are not speaking. When you sin or neglect worship, does your heart still hold that faith, or have you allowed it to weaken? What is one thing you can do tonight to reconnect with that inner reality?
?
If the reality of faith is permanent in the heart, why do you still feel distant from God at times? What are you willing to sacrifice to ensure your heart remains the true abode of faith, not just your tongue?

Sin Does Not Remove Faith: Quranic Evidence
Maturidi cites rebuke verses to prove sin does not annul faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic rebuke verses to prove that sin does not expel a believer from the fold of faith.

Core Idea
The Quran rebukes believers as 'believers'—sin does not remove faith.

Imam Maturidi refutes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila who claim that major sins remove a person from faith. He cites four Quranic verses where Allah rebukes believers for their shortcomings yet still addresses them as 'O you who believe'. This shows that the name of faith remains despite sin, invalidating those sects' positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the four Quranic verses
Identify the four verses Maturidi cites: 'O you who believe, why do you say what you do not do...', 'O you who believe, what is the matter with you...', 'And what is the matter with you that you do not fight...', 'Has not the time come for those who believe...'.
All verses begin with 'O you who believe'.
2
Observe the rebuke and the title
Notice that Allah rebukes them for sinful actions but still calls them 'believers'. He does not remove the name of faith.
This is the key point.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi argues that if sin removed faith, the rebuke would not use the title 'believers'. Therefore, the Khawarij and Mu'tazila are wrong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى هذا النوع آيات هي تنقض على المعتزلة والخوارج والكرامية والحشوية مذهبهم على اختلاف مذاهبهم نحو قوله: (يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ) إلى قوله: (كَأَنَّهُمْ بُنْيَانٌ مَرْصُوصٌ)، وقوله تعالى: (يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مَا لَكُمْ إِذَا قِيلَ لَكُمُ انْفِرُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ)، وقوله تعالى: (وَمَا لَكُمْ لا تُقَاتِلُونَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَالمُسْتَضْعَفِينَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ)، وقوله تعالى: (أَلَمْ يَأْنِ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ تَخْشَعَ قُلُوبُهُم لِذِكْرِ اللهِ)، فعاتب عز وجل على صنيعهم ذلك وأعظم العيد في ذلك ولم يزل عنهم اسم الإيمان بل به عاتبهم، وكذلك في العقل تكون معاتبة بالتقصير يكون بين الأولياء، ويكون بين الأعداء محاجة ومحاربة، فبان قد بقى لهم اسم الإيمان، فيبطل قول من يخرج من الإيمان وقول من يكفره، كذلك إذ لا أحد التبس عليه تضمنه تلك الآيات ممن يصدق بالله وبرسوله الإيمان اسم لمعروف الحد، وأن كلا ممن ذلك لسانه يعقل، فيبطل قول من يقول: الإيمان اسم جميع الطاعات ما ذلك الخطاب على ترك من الفرائض، فلو كان اسما للكل لكانوا: يا أيها الذين آمنوا ببعض الإيمان، أو آمنوا مع الثنيا فيه. وكما لا يصلح في مثل ذلك المعاتبة باسم الأبرار التقين، ثبت أن الإيمان اسم للخاص من العبادات لا للكل. ثم لا أحد منهم وقت نزول الآية يعرف منهم استعمال اللسان بذلك، ثبت أن التسمية كانت بالقلب، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And in this category there are verses that refute the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Karramiyya, and Hashwiyya in their various doctrines. For example His saying: 'O you who believe, why do you say what you do not do?' to His saying: 'as if they were a well-built wall,' and His saying: 'O you who believe, what is the matter with you that when it is said to you: march forth in the way of God,' and His saying: 'And what is the matter with you that you do not fight in the way of God and the oppressed among men, women, and children,' and His saying: 'Has not the time come for those who believe that their hearts should become humble for the remembrance of God?' So He, may He be glorified and exalted, rebuked them for their actions and made the rebuke great in that, and He did not remove from them the name of faith; rather, He rebuked them with it. Similarly, in the intellect, rebuke for deficiency occurs between allies, and between enemies there is argument and war. So it is clear that the name of faith remained with them; thus the statement of those who expel from faith and the statement of those who declare him a disbeliever are invalidated. Similarly, since no one who believes in God and His Messenger is confused about the import of those verses – that faith is a name with a known limit, and that everyone whose tongue does that is rational – so the statement of those who say: 'faith is the name for all acts of obedience' is invalidated. For that address (to believers who are rebuked) would have required them to have left some duties. If it (faith) were a name for all (acts), then they would be addressed as 'O you who believe with partial faith' or 'believe with exception'. And just as it is not appropriate in such rebuke to use the name of the righteous, it is established that faith is a name for a specific act of worship, not for all. Furthermore, none of them at the time of the revelation of the verse is known to have used the tongue for that; so it is established that the naming was by the heart. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 978

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of multiple sects on the nature of faith. Maturidi cites four Quranic verses where believers are rebuked for their shortcomings (saying what they do not do, hesitation to fight, lack of humility). In each case, God addresses them as 'O you who believe' and rebukes them, but does not strip them of the title 'believers'. This proves that sin does not remove faith entirely, refuting the Mu'tazila and Khawarij who claim major sins expel from faith. Additionally, the fact that God rebukes them for failing to perform certain duties (e.g., fighting) shows that faith is not the name for all acts of obedience; if it were, these people would have had complete faith (since they are called believers) and could not be rebuked for missing duties. Rather, their faith remains but they are deficient in other acts. Maturidi then argues that if faith meant all acts, then the address would have to be 'O you who believe with partial faith' or 'believe with exception', which is not the case. Nor is it appropriate to rebuke them as if they were the righteous. Therefore, faith is a specific act (the inner conviction) not the totality of good deeds. Finally, he notes that at the time of revelation, no one was known to have used their tongue to express faith in that specific moment, so the naming must be based on the heart. This passage systematically refutes the idea that faith is merely speech (Karramiyya, Hashwiyya extremes) or that faith is all acts (some Mu'tazili view) or that sin annuls faith (Khawarij).

Key Terms
الإيمان
المعتزلة
الخوارج
الكرامية
الحشوية
المعاتبة
اسم الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that committing a major sin removes one from the fold of faith entirely.
Correction: The Quranic verses show that Allah rebukes believers for sins while still calling them 'believers', proving sin does not expel from faith.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi use the rebuke verses to refute the Khawarij and Mu'tazila?
A) By showing that believers rebuked for sin are still called believers, so sin does not expel from faith.
B) By arguing that rebuke proves they are not believers.
C) By claiming that sin is impossible for a true believer.
D) By saying that rebuke only applies to hypocrites.

Key Takeaway
Sin does not remove the name of faith; the Quran itself calls sinners 'believers' while rebuking them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you still consider yourself a believer, or do you feel that your faith is completely lost? Does the way Allah addresses you as 'O you who believe' in the Quran change how you view yourself after falling into sin? Commit to one concrete change in how you respond to Allah's rebuke.
?
Maturidi explains that rebuke between allies is different from argument with enemies. Think of a recent sin you committed. Did you respond to Allah's rebuke (e.g., guilt, Quranic reminders) as an ally or as an enemy? What would it look like to receive rebuke as a beloved believer who is being corrected out of love?
?
The Quran calls you 'believer' even when you slip. Does that encourage you to obey more or give you an excuse to sin? Be honest: Which has it been in your life? Resolve today to let the name of faith motivate obedience, not complacency.

Faith and Disbelief

Faith is a Specific Act, Not All Acts
Maturidi argues faith is not all acts, but a specific act of worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that faith is a specific act of worship (inner assent) and not the sum of all acts of obedience.

Core Idea
If faith were all acts, rebuke for missing duties would be contradictory.

Imam Maturidi continues his refutation, now targeting those who say faith is the name for all acts of obedience (such as some Mu'tazila and Hashwiyya). He argues that if faith meant all acts, then the believers rebuked in the verses would have to be addressed as 'O you who believe with partial faith' or 'believe with exception', which is not the case. Therefore, faith must be a specific act—the inner conviction—not the totality of deeds.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim refuted
Some groups say faith is the name for all acts of obedience. Maturidi refutes this.
This is opposed to the Khawarij view but also wrong.
2
Follow the logical argument
If faith were all acts, then the rebuked believers would have missed some duties, so their faith would be incomplete. The address 'O you who believe' would be inappropriate unless qualified.
The absence of qualification shows faith is not all acts.
3
Note the heart-based naming
Maturidi concludes that faith is by the heart, not the tongue, since no one at revelation time was known to have used the tongue for that naming.

?

Have you ever comforted yourself with your deeds while neglecting the heartfelt conviction that is the essence of īmān? Will you today examine whether your inner reliance on Allah is alive, or merely assumed because you perform duties?
?
The Quran rebukes believers for leaving duties, yet still calls them believers. When you fall short in obedience, do you despair that your faith is lost, or do you take it as a call to strengthen the inner act that remains? How can you this week focus on the core of īmān – tawḥīd and submission of the heart – rather than resting on your compliance?

The Meaning of Irja' and Refutation of the Hashwiyya
Maturidi defines irja' and refutes a sectarian claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic meaning of irja' and how Maturidi refutes a sectarian misinterpretation.

Core Idea
The name 'Murji'ah' comes from postponement, not from their view on good deeds.

Maturidi begins by establishing the agreed-upon linguistic meaning of irja' as postponement, citing Quranic usage. He then addresses a claim by the Hashwiyya that the Murji'ah were named because they did not count all good deeds as iman. Through language and reason, he shows this claim is baseless, reinforcing that the name is rooted in the concept of postponement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: first the linguistic consensus, then the Hashwiyya's claim, then Maturidi's refutation.
2
Identify the key claim and refutation
Find where Maturidi states the Hashwiyya's claim and his response. He first says it is not supported by language or reason, then explains why linguistically.
The refutation uses both language and reason.
3
Understand the linguistic argument
Maturidi explains that irja' means postponement, and there is no basis for naming a group based on their not applying a general name (iman) to each specific good deed. This is a linguistic argument.
4
Reflect on the logical dilemma
Maturidi ends with a logical point: either the name 'Murji'' applies to everything or not. If it does, why object? This forces the reader to see the inconsistency of the Hashwiyya's position.
The passage ends abruptly, but the argument is complete in its direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: في الإرجاء ثم اختلف في المعنى الذي سمي به من سمي مُرجئاً بعد اتفاق أهل اللسان على الإرجاء أنه التأخير، وعلى ذلك قوله: أرجه وأرجاه، وقال: مرجون لأمر الله. قالت الحشوية: سميت المرجئة بما لم يسموا كل الخيرات إيمانا. وهذا لا يحتمله اللسان ولا العقل. فأما اللسان فهو أن الإرجاء هو التأخير، ولا وجه الاسم فيما يسمى كل خير باسمه الخاص ومنع هذا الاسم العام. ثم لا يخلو أن يكون هذا في الحقيقة اسما لكل أو لا، فإن كان اسما له فمن يأبى تسمية هذا.
Question: Concerning irja'. Then they differed about the meaning by which the one called Murji' was named, after the people of language agreed that irja' means postponement. And on that is His saying: "Postpone him and his brothers" and He said: "Those who are deferred for the command of Allah." The Hashwiyya said: The Murji'ah were named because they did not count all good deeds as iman. But this is not borne by language nor by reason. As for language, irja' is postponement, and there is no aspect for the name in that one calls every good deed by its specific name and forbids this general name. Then it does not escape that this is either in reality a name for everything or not. If it is a name for it, then who would refuse to name this?
Source pages p. 980

Commentary
This passage is a clarification and refutation. Maturidi begins by stating that after the people of language agreed that irja' means postponement, there was disagreement about the meaning for which someone is called 'Murji' (one who postpones). He cites Quranic usage: 'Postpone him and his brothers' (referring to the story of the hypocrites in Surah al-A'raf?) and 'Those who are deferred for the command of Allah' (Quran 9:106). Then he reports the claim of the Hashwiyya (a sect that adhered to literalist hadith interpretation) that the Murji'ah were so named because they did not count all good deeds as iman. Maturidi rejects this claim as linguistically and rationally unsound. He explains the linguistic point: irja' means postponement, and there is no basis for calling a group by that name simply because they do not apply the name 'iman' to all good deeds. He then poses a logical dilemma: either the name (i.e., calling someone Murji') is in reality a name for everything (i.e., for all matters related to postponement) or it is not. If it is a general name, then why would anyone object to applying it? The passage ends abruptly, but the point is that the Hashwiyya's explanation is invalid. The correct meaning is that the Murji'ah are those who postpone deeds from the domain of iman (i.e., they say iman is only belief, not deeds, so deeds are delayed in judgment).

Key Terms
إرجاء
مرجئ
مرجئة
الحشوية
اللسان
العقل
تأخير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Murji'ah are named because they exclude good deeds from iman.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the name comes from the linguistic meaning 'postponement', not from any doctrinal stance on good deeds.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue is the correct linguistic meaning of 'irja'?
A) Counting all good deeds as iman.
B) Postponement.
C) Denial of good deeds.
D) Innovation.

Key Takeaway
The name Murji'ah is rooted in the linguistic meaning of postponement, not in their theological view about faith and deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a label for a group of Muslims based on a misunderstanding of what they actually believe? How can you ensure your judgments are grounded in accurate definitions like Maturidi insists?
?
The Hashwiyya made a claim about the Murji'ah without checking the linguistic reality. In your own life, are there claims about others that you have accepted without verifying their basis in language or reason? What will you do to correct that?
?
Maturidi uses both language and reason to correct a mistaken naming. When it comes to your own understanding of theological terms, are you willing to be corrected by language and reason, even if it challenges your assumptions? Is there a label you hold about a group that you need to reexamine?

Divine Mercy and Justice in Punishment
Maturidi outlines two divine possibilities for sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible outcomes God may decree for a believer's sins: either expiation through good deeds or exact justice.

Core Idea
God balances mercy and justice; He may forgive through expiation or hold accountable with perfect justice.

Maturidi begins by affirming God's attributes of forgiveness and mercy. He then presents two possibilities for how God treats the sins of believers: either good deeds expiate sins (based on Quranic promises) or each deed is rewarded and punished precisely. This sets the stage for understanding legitimate deferral of judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine attributes and expiation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the opening attributes and the Quranic verses.
The passage contains multiple verse citations; don't get bogged down in details yet.
2
Identify the two divine wills mentioned
The passage presents two possible actions of God regarding sin. Find where 'if He wills' appears and what follows.
One option involves expiation, the other precise recompense.
3
Examine the Quranic verses cited for expiation
List the verses that support expiation. Understand how they relate to God's mercy.
Verses include 11:114, 4:31, 46:16, 29:7.
4
Reflect on the description of justice in retribution
The second option is described as justice. Consider how this relates to God's attribute of justice.
Maturidi says this description of justice is valid even though God is the bestower of reward.

ذ قال : هو الغفور وهو الرحيم الودود، وإن شاء قابل بسيئته ما أكرمه به من الحسنات فجعلهن كفارات لها كما قال تعالى: {إِنَّ الْحَسَنَاتِ يُذْهِبْنَ السَّيِّئَاتِ}، قال في غير موضع: {نُكَفِّرْ عَنْكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ}، وقد ذكر الأنواع التي وعد نها التكفير، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وذلك كقوله: {أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ نَتَقَبَّلُ عَنْهُمْ أَحْسَنَ مَا عَمِلُوا وَنَتَجَاوَزُ عَنْ سَيِّئَاتِهِمْ}، وقوله: {وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَنُكَفِّرَنَّ عَنْهُمْ سَيِّئَاتِهِمْ}، ذلك، والله أعلم. وإن شاء جزاه قدر عمله، وما كان منه من الحسنات فقدرها أيضا بقوله: {فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ}، وغير ذلك من الآيات التي فيها ذكر جزاء الخير والشر، وذلك وصف العدل في المؤاخذة وإن كان هو الثواب مفضلا، وبالله التوفيق. وهذا النوع من الإرجاء حق لزم القول به. والمعتزلة أرجت فعل نفسه حيث أبى تسميته مؤمنا وكافرا، فجهله بحقيقته ألزمه القول بإرجاء الاسم، لكنه جهل حقيقة فعله فلا عذر له، والأول جهل حقيقة ما يعمل به الله، وذلك لا يعرف إلا بالسمع، ولم يجىء ما يقطع القول بشيء فهو لازم.
He said: He is the Forgiving, the Merciful, the Loving. And if He wills, He may compare his evil deed with the good deeds He honored him with and make them expiations for it, as He said: {Indeed, good deeds remove evil deeds} (11:114). He said in another place: {We will expiate for you your evil deeds} (4:31). And He mentioned the types which He promised expiation. And there is no power except with Allah. And that is like His saying: {Those are the ones from whom We will accept the best of what they did and overlook their misdeeds} (46:16), and His saying: {And those who believe and do righteous deeds, We will surely expiate for them their misdeeds} (29:7). That, and Allah knows best. And if He wills, He may reward him according to his deed, and whatever good deeds he had, He also apportions them according to His saying: {So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it} (99:7), and other verses mentioning the reward of good and evil. And that is a description of justice in taking to account, although He is the bestower of reward, and with Allah is success. And this type of irja' is true and necessary to affirm. And the Mu'tazila deferred (arjat) their own action when they refused to call him a believer or disbeliever, so his ignorance of its reality compelled him to say that the name is deferred, but he was ignorant of the reality of his action, so he has no excuse. And the first [type] is ignorance of the reality of what Allah does, and that is not known except through revelation, and nothing has come that decisively cuts off speech, so it is necessary.
Source pages p. 982

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of legitimate irja'. Maturidi cites divine attributes of forgiveness and mercy, and verses indicating that good deeds expiate evil deeds. He distinguishes between two wills of God: either He forgives by making good deeds expiate sins, or He rewards precisely according to deeds, which is an act of justice, though He is also the bestower of reward. This type of irja'—deferring to God's will—is obligatory to affirm. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for deferring the judgment on the sinner's name (whether believer or disbeliever) due to ignorance of the reality of the action. This ignorance is blameworthy because it stems from not knowing the true nature of the action. In contrast, the first type of irja' (deferring to God's will regarding punishment) is based on revelation, and since no decisive text exists to definitively state the eternal fate of the major sinner, it is necessary to defer. Thus, the legitimate irja' is grounded in scripture, not ignorance.

الغفور
الرحيم
الودود
الحسنات
السيئات
التكفير
العدل

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses is NOT cited by Maturidi in this passage regarding expiation?
A) {Indeed, good deeds remove evil deeds} (11:114)
B) {We will expiate for you your evil deeds} (4:31)
C) {And those who believe and do righteous deeds, We will surely expiate for them their misdeeds} (29:7)
D) {And whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it} (99:8)

Key Takeaway
God may either forgive sins through good deeds or hold accountable with justice; both are possible under His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your good deeds automatically cancel out your sins, forgetting that it is entirely up to Allah's will? How does this lesson challenge that assumption and what will you do differently today?
?
Knowing that Allah may either forgive through expiation or hold you to exact justice, what specific sin are you relying on His mercy for, and what concrete step will you take to increase your good deeds as an act of hope, not entitlement?
?
The passage describes justice in taking to account while also affirming that Allah is the bestower of reward. Does your heart truly rest in the balance of both, or do you lean too heavily on one side? What would it mean for you to live with genuine hope and genuine accountability simultaneously?
