Maturidi's Refutation of the Distinction between Iman and Islam
Maturidi refutes the distinction between iman and Islam through logical questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical argument that distinguishing between iman and Islam leads to inconsistency and is therefore invalid.

Core Idea
A distinction without a difference is mere confusion.

Imam Maturidi directly addresses those who claim that iman (faith) and Islam (submission) are distinct categories. He challenges them to show a practical difference in rulings. This passage exposes the logical flaw in their position by asking a series of questions that cannot be consistently answered.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Maturidi begins by addressing the proponent of the distinction.
2
Identify the key question
Maturidi asks whether the distinction results in different actual rulings in this world and the Hereafter. Find this question in the text.
3
Understand the logical trap
Maturidi then asks specific questions about which abode the Muslim or believer belongs to, which name is more praiseworthy, and what rights are established by one name but not the other. The distinguisher cannot provide consistent answers.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since no consistent difference can be shown, Maturidi concludes that the distinction is arbitrary and confuses matters. The distinguisher is merely a 'frivolous confuser.'
The passage ends with a marginal note; the core argument ends before it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لصاحب هذا القول: تحقق هذا الاسم بأحدهما ويمنع الآخر حكماً في أمر الدنيا والآخرة أو لا، فإن حقق فيقال: ما ذلك إلى أي الدارين المسلم أو المؤمن؟ ثم في الشاهد أي الاسمين أحمد، وأي حق فيما بين العبد وربه أو بينه وبين الخلق تحقق له عند وجود أحد الأسمين ولا تحقق عند وجود الآخر؟ فلا يجد إلى تحقيق ذلك سبيلاً. فيرد فيقال عند ذلك: إذ لم يجعل الاسم بأحدهما علماً لأمر منعت المسمى بالآخر، وكذلك فيما يلحق الضرر، فإذا صرت أنت بالتفريق عابثاً ملبساً. [۷] جاءت في الأصل على هامش النص مع الإشارة إلى أنها من صلب النص. ن سال ها به اسلام و الالوان البرية
Then it is said to the proponent of this saying: Do you actualize this name by one of them and prevent the other in terms of ruling in the matters of this world and the Hereafter, or not? If he actualizes, then it is said: What is that? To which of the two abodes does the Muslim or the believer belong? Then in the witnessed world, which of the two names is more praiseworthy, and what right, between the servant and his Lord or between him and the creation, is actualized for him when one of the two names exists but not actualized when the other exists? He will find no way to actualize that. So it is said in reply at that point: Since you have not made the name by one of them a sign for a matter that prevents the one named by the other, and likewise regarding harm, then you, through distinction, become a frivolous confuser. [7] It occurs in the original on the margin of the text with the indication that it is from the body of the text. n sal ha bi islam wa al-alwan al-bariyya [unclear].
Source pages p. 997

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. Maturidi directly addresses the one who distinguishes between iman and Islam. He asks a series of penetrating questions: Do you actually give the ruling based on one name and deny it based on the other? If you do, then what is that ruling? Does the Muslim belong to a different abode than the believer? In this world, which name is more praiseworthy? What rights are established for one name but not the other? The distinguisher cannot provide a consistent answer. Therefore, since he has not made the name a sign for a distinct ruling, his distinction is arbitrary and leads to confusion. Maturidi concludes that the distinguisher is merely playing with words and causing confusion. The final unclear line appears to be an editorial note or marginal comment, possibly in Persian, and does not affect the main argument.

Key Terms
صاحب القول (proponent)
تفريق (distinction)
تحقيق (actualization)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the distinction between iman and Islam is a real theological difference with different rulings.
Correction: Maturidi shows that no consistent ruling can be assigned to each name, proving the distinction is invalid.

Checkpoint
What is Maturidi's main argument against the one who distinguishes between iman and Islam?
A) That the distinguisher cannot consistently assign different rulings to each name
B) That the Quran never mentions both terms
C) That the hadith forbid distinguishing
D) That the scholars all agree on distinction

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves that the claimed distinction between iman and Islam is untenable because it cannot be consistently applied to real-world rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever separated your faith from your actions in practice, considering yourself a believer but neglecting the obligations of Islam? How does Maturidi's refutation challenge that separation?
?
Reflect on a time when you made a distinction in your heart that had no real effect on how you lived. What does this passage say about the danger of making such distinctions without grounding?
?
How does the accusation of being a 'frivolous confuser' apply to your own theological discussions? Are you more concerned with terminology than with the actual rulings and realities of faith?

The Three Categories and the Instinctive Meaning of Islam
Maturidi starts with historical categories and the linguistic nature of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in the Prophet's time there were only three categories (believer, disbeliever, hypocrite) and that Islam has an innate meaning that cannot be reduced or expanded.

Core Idea
Islam is not a separate category; it is known by natural disposition.

Imam Maturidi begins his argument by recalling the simple social reality of early Islam: people were either believers, disbelievers, or hypocrites. There was no intermediate 'Muslim' category apart from these. He then notes that even those who rejected Islam instinctively knew its meaning, as evidenced by their aversion to the name. This sets the stage for his proof that Islam and iman are identical in essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the three categories
Identify the three groups mentioned: believer (mu'min), disbeliever (kafir), and hypocrite (munafiq).
There is no fourth group called 'Muslim' separate from these.
2
Observe the linguistic argument about the name 'Islam'
Notice that all religious communities fled from the name 'Islam', implying they knew its meaning instinctively.
This shows Islam is not an arbitrary label.
3
Understand the dilemma of adding or subtracting meaning
If Islam is less than iman, one could be a Muslim without being a believer—contradiction. If more, then aversion to Islam would not occur as it does.
The dilemma proves Islam and iman are neither more nor less than each other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الناس في عهد رسول الله ثلاثة : مؤمن وكافر ومنافق ، لم يُعرف للمسلم درجة خارجة من هؤلاء ولا للمؤمن ، وفي التفريق ذلك ، وذلك خلاف ما عليه الأمر الأول من الخلق . على أن أهل الأديان جميعا فروا عن اسم الإسلام ، فلو أنه ما معناه وما الذي نفر عنه يكن الاسلام معروفا عند طباعهم معنى لذلك ، وبه وصف الرسل أنهم سموا . وإذا ثبت أنه معلوم عند الخلق ، فمن رام صرفه إلى معنى زائد في الدين أو إلى معنى زائد على الإيمان أو ناقص كان لا يجب أن ذهب إلى معنى ناقص عنه أن يجعل الإسلام دون الإيمان فيجب حقيقته والتدين بذلك الدين ، ثم لا يكون مؤمنا . وإن كان زائدا فيجب أن لا يقع النفار عن قدر ما يدعون إلى الإيمان وإن لم يوصف لهم أنه أسلم ، فإذ وجد ذلك ثبت أن معنى ذلك غير زائد على الآخر ولا له وجود دونه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من بدل دينه فاقتلوه ، ثم بين الله دينه فقال : فَمَنْ يَكْفُرْ بِالطَّاغُوتِ وَيُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ ، فيقال : أهو مسلم أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، فقد بدل إذا دين الله ، وإن قال : نعم ، صار مسلما يفعل الإيمان لا غير. على أن هذا الخبر في تبديل الدين ، وأنه معروف أنه الاعتقاد لا غير ، وأن المراد في ذلك راجع إلى الدين الذي هو الإسلام ، ثبت أنه معروف الحد والقدر يعرف مبدله ، ولو كانت الأفعال سوى الاعتقاد دينا كان كل واحد في كل أحواله مبدل الدين لوجود تلك الأفعال أفعال من القرب في كل وقت ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال له : الخبر الذي رويت في هذا الباب في تفسير الإسلام فيه ذكر الأمور الظاهرة ، وكذلك أهل النفاق يوافقون المؤمنين في الأمور الظاهرة ، وقد . نعم : قيل لهم : قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ، أهو الإسلام في الحقيقة أو لا ؟ فإن قال : الإسلام في الحقيقة صير قوله : إِنَّ الدِّينَ عِنْدَ اللهِ الإِسْلَامُ ، وقوله : وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامِ دِينًا هو الذي ذكر، فيجب أن يكون قوله : وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الإسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ فِي الآخِرَةِ مِنَ الخَاسِرِينَ ، وقال : وَكَيْفَ يَهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمًا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إِيمَانِهِم ، هو ذلك الذي قال لهم: قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ، وما جاء به الخبر لوجود تلك الشهادة في أهل النفاق وتلك الأفعال عنهم فيكون المخلصون والمؤمنون قد ابتغوا غير الإسلام دينا ، وتركوا ما رضى الله وأهل النفاق الذين جاءوا به ، وذلك بعيد. فثبت أن ذلك الإسلام الانقياد والاستسلام ، وأما حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة لا ما ذكر من الظواهر ، دليل ذلك الأمر الذي ذكروا أن الله قال في آخر السورة : يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُلْ لا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكُم ولو كان الإسلام ما أظهروا كيف قال : إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ . ثم فيه أنه جعلهم مسلمين كما قالوا إن هدوا للإيمان لا بما أظهروا ، ثبت أن الإيمان هو الإسلام. وكذلك قال : وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الإسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَنْ يُقبَلُ مِنْهُ ، ثم بين ذلك الدين الذي هو الإسلام وقال:
The people in the era of the Messenger of God were three: a believer, a disbeliever, and a hypocrite. No degree outside these was known for the Muslim, nor for the believer, and in that differentiation, and that is contrary to what the first state of creation was. But all the people of religions fled from the name of Islam. If only it were known what its meaning is and what they fled from, Islam would be known in their natures as a meaning for that, and by it the messengers were described that they were named. And when it is established that it is known among creation, then whoever aims to divert it to an additional meaning in religion or to a meaning additional to iman or deficient, it would be necessary that if he goes to a deficient meaning he would make Islam inferior to iman, so its reality and adherence to that religion would be necessary, then he would not be a believer. And if it were additional, it would be necessary that the aversion would not occur to the extent they call to iman even if they were not described as having submitted. So when that is found, it is established that its meaning is not additional to the other nor does it have existence without it, and there is no power except with God. And the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' Then God clarified His religion and said: 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in God...' So it is said: Is he a Muslim or not? If he says: No, then he has changed the religion of God; and if he says: Yes, he becomes a Muslim doing iman alone. This report is about changing the religion, and it is known that it is belief alone, and that what is intended in that refers to the religion which is Islam. It is established that it is known in limit and measure, and its changer is known. And if deeds other than belief were a religion, then every person in all his states would be a changer of the religion due to the existence of those deeds, deeds of closeness, at every time, and there is no power except with God. Then it is said to him: The report you narrated in this chapter about the explanation of Islam mentions outward matters, and likewise the hypocrites agree with the believers in outward matters, and so. Yes: It was said to them: 'Say: We have submitted (aslamna), is that Islam in reality or not?' If he says: It is Islam in reality, then his saying: 'Indeed the religion with God is Islam,' and His saying: 'And I have chosen for you Islam as a religion,' would make that the one mentioned, so it would be necessary that His saying: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him, and in the Hereafter he will be among the losers,' and His saying: 'How will God guide a people who disbelieved after their belief,' would be that which He said to them: 'Say: We have submitted,' and what the report brought due to the existence of that testimony among the hypocrites and those deeds from them, so the sincere ones and the believers would have sought a religion other than Islam and abandoned what God was pleased with, and the hypocrites who brought it, and that is far-fetched. So it is established that that Islam is submission and surrender (al-inqiyad wa al-istislam), and as for its reality, it is the religion in reality, not what is mentioned of outward signs. The evidence for that is the matter which they mentioned that God said at the end of the surah: 'They regard it as a favor to you that they have submitted (aslamu). Say: Do not count your Islam as a favor to me...' And if Islam were what they showed outwardly, how could He say: 'If you are truthful'? Then in it is that He made them Muslims as they said, if they were guided to iman, not by what they showed outwardly. It is established that iman is Islam. Likewise He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him,' then He explained that religion which is Islam and said:
Source pages p. 998

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument by Imam al-Maturidi proving that Islam and iman (faith) are identical in their essential reality, and that mere outward actions do not constitute true Islam. He begins by noting that people in the Prophet's time fell into only three categories: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite—there was no intermediate degree for the Muslim separate from the believer. He then observes that all religious communities originally recoiled from the name 'Islam', implying that its meaning is instinctively known. Whoever tries to add or subtract from that meaning faces a dilemma: if Islam is less than iman, then one could be a Muslim without being a believer, which contradicts the Prophet's classification; if it is more, then the aversion to it would not occur as it does. Thus the meanings are not distinct. Next, he cites the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' and the verse 'whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God'. If asked whether such a person is Muslim, saying no makes him a changer of God's religion, but saying yes implies he is a Muslim solely through iman. Therefore the religion meant is belief itself, not actions; otherwise everyone would constantly be changing religion by performing different deeds. The second part addresses an objection: the hadith about Islam mentions outward acts, and hypocrites also perform them. But the verse 'Say: We have submitted' (from Surah al-Hujurat) is questioned: is that submission true Islam? If yes, then other verses like 'The religion with God is Islam' would condemn sincere believers for seeking another religion. This is absurd. Thus the true nature of Islam is inward submission (al-inqiyad wa al-istislam), not outward shows. The proof is that God rebukes the Bedouins for claiming submission when they are not truthful, and He makes them Muslims only if they are guided to iman, i.e., inward faith. Therefore iman and Islam are one and the same.

Key Terms
إسلام
إيمان
منافق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Islam is a separate category from iman, perhaps less demanding.
Correction: Maturidi shows Islam and iman are identical in essence; there is no intermediate degree.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the fact that people flee from the name 'Islam' prove it is known instinctively?
A) Because they have studied Islam deeply
B) Because flight requires recognition of what one is fleeing
C) Because the Prophet taught them
D) Because it is a foreign word

Key Takeaway
Islam and iman are not different categories; they share the same reality, as shown by the absence of a fourth category and the instinctive knowledge of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may call yourself a Muslim, but do you feel the same aversion to the name 'Islam' as those who flee from it? What does your comfort with the label reveal about the state of your heart's submission?
?
If Islam and iman are identical, then your outward actions are not separate from your inner faith. Are you living as if your deeds can be disconnected from your belief? What would change if you truly embraced their unity?
?
The Prophet's era had only three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. Which of these do you most resemble in your current state, and what specific step must you take today to move toward true iman?

The Hadith on Changing Religion and the Reductio on Deeds
Maturidi uses the hadith on changing religion to show religion is only belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' proves that the religion (Islam) is inward belief, not outward actions.

Core Idea
If deeds were part of religion, everyone would constantly be changing religion.

Maturidi now deploys a well-known hadith: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' He connects it to a Quranic verse that defines religion as belief in God and rejection of taghut. He then poses a simple question: if a person meets this criterion, is he a Muslim? The answer leads to a reductio ad absurdum that shows deeds cannot be constitutive of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its implication
The hadith prescribes killing for changing religion. Understand that this punishment assumes religion is a well-defined, non-negotiable entity.
The hadith is about 'religion' (din), which Maturidi equates with Islam.
2
Analyze the question and its answer
The verse on disbelieving in taghut and believing in God is presented. If asked if such a person is Muslim, saying no means he changed religion; saying yes makes him a Muslim by belief alone.
This indicates that Islam is solely defined by belief, not by additional outward acts.
3
Understand the reductio about deeds
If deeds (actions, acts of worship) were part of religion, then every variation in deeds would constitute a change of religion. Since people constantly perform different actions, everyone would be guilty of changing religion daily.
This is absurd, confirming that deeds are not part of the essence of Islam.

لهم : قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ، أهو الإسلام في الحقيقة أو لا ؟ فإن قال : الإسلام في الحقيقة صير قوله : إِنَّ الدِّينَ عِنْدَ اللهِ الإِسْلَامُ ، وقوله : وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامِ دِينًا هو الذي ذكر، فيجب أن يكون قوله : وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الإسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ فِي الآخِرَةِ مِنَ الخَاسِرِينَ ، وقال : وَكَيْفَ يَهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمًا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إِيمَانِهِم ، هو ذلك الذي قال لهم: قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ، وما جاء به الخبر لوجود تلك الشهادة في أهل النفاق وتلك الأفعال عنهم فيكون المخلصون والمؤمنون قد ابتغوا غير الإسلام دينا ، وتركوا ما رضى الله وأهل النفاق الذين جاءوا به ، وذلك بعيد. فثبت أن ذلك الإسلام الانقياد والاستسلام ، وأما حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة لا ما ذكر من الظواهر ، دليل ذلك الأمر الذي ذكروا أن الله قال في آخر السورة : يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُلْ لا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكُم ولو كان الإسلام ما أظهروا كيف قال : إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ . ثم فيه أنه جعلهم مسلمين كما قالوا إن هدوا للإيمان لا بما أظهروا ، ثبت أن الإيمان هو الإسلام. وكذلك قال : وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الإسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَنْ يُقبَلُ مِنْهُ ، ثم بين ذلك الدين الذي هو الإسلام وقال:
The people in the era of the Messenger of God were three: a believer, a disbeliever, and a hypocrite. No degree outside these was known for the Muslim, nor for the believer, and in that differentiation, and that is contrary to what the first state of creation was. But all the people of religions fled from the name of Islam. If only it were known what its meaning is and what they fled from, Islam would be known in their natures as a meaning for that, and by it the messengers were described that they were named. And when it is established that it is known among creation, then whoever aims to divert it to an additional meaning in religion or to a meaning additional to iman or deficient, it would be necessary that if he goes to a deficient meaning he would make Islam inferior to iman, so its reality and adherence to that religion would be necessary, then he would not be a believer. And if it were additional, it would be necessary that the aversion would not occur to the extent they call to iman even if they were not described as having submitted. So when that is found, it is established that its meaning is not additional to the other nor does it have existence without it, and there is no power except with God. And the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' Then God clarified His religion and said: 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in God...' So it is said: Is he a Muslim or not? If he says: No, then he has changed the religion of God; and if he says: Yes, he becomes a Muslim doing iman alone. This report is about changing the religion, and it is known that it is belief alone, and that what is intended in that refers to the religion which is Islam. It is established that it is known in limit and measure, and its changer is known. And if deeds other than belief were a religion, then every person in all his states would be a changer of the religion due to the existence of those deeds, deeds of closeness, at every time, and there is no power except with God. Then it is said to him: The report you narrated in this chapter about the explanation of Islam mentions outward matters, and likewise the hypocrites agree with the believers in outward matters, and so. Yes: It was said to them: 'Say: We have submitted (aslamna), is that Islam in reality or not?' If he says: It is Islam in reality, then his saying: 'Indeed the religion with God is Islam,' and His saying: 'And I have chosen for you Islam as a religion,' would make that the one mentioned, so it would be necessary that His saying: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him, and in the Hereafter he will be among the losers,' and His saying: 'How will God guide a people who disbelieved after their belief,' would be that which He said to them: 'Say: We have submitted,' and what the report brought due to the existence of that testimony among the hypocrites and those deeds from them, so the sincere ones and the believers would have sought a religion other than Islam and abandoned what God was pleased with, and the hypocrites who brought it, and that is far-fetched. So it is established that that Islam is submission and surrender (al-inqiyad wa al-istislam), and as for its reality, it is the religion in reality, not what is mentioned of outward signs. The evidence for that is the matter which they mentioned that God said at the end of the surah: 'They regard it as a favor to you that they have submitted (aslamu). Say: Do not count your Islam as a favor to me...' And if Islam were what they showed outwardly, how could He say: 'If you are truthful'? Then in it is that He made them Muslims as they said, if they were guided to iman, not by what they showed outwardly. It is established that iman is Islam. Likewise He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him,' then He explained that religion which is Islam and said:
Source pages p. 998

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument by Imam al-Maturidi proving that Islam and iman (faith) are identical in their essential reality, and that mere outward actions do not constitute true Islam. He begins by noting that people in the Prophet's time fell into only three categories: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite—there was no intermediate degree for the Muslim separate from the believer. He then observes that all religious communities originally recoiled from the name 'Islam', implying that its meaning is instinctively known. Whoever tries to add or subtract from that meaning faces a dilemma: if Islam is less than iman, then one could be a Muslim without being a believer, which contradicts the Prophet's classification; if it is more, then the aversion to it would not occur as it does. Thus the meanings are not distinct. Next, he cites the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' and the verse 'whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God'. If asked whether such a person is Muslim, saying no makes him a changer of God's religion, but saying yes implies he is a Muslim solely through iman. Therefore the religion meant is belief itself, not actions; otherwise everyone would constantly be changing religion by performing different deeds. The second part addresses an objection: the hadith about Islam mentions outward acts, and hypocrites also perform them. But the verse 'Say: We have submitted' (from Surah al-Hujurat) is questioned: is that submission true Islam? If yes, then other verses like 'The religion with God is Islam' would condemn sincere believers for seeking another religion. This is absurd. Thus the true nature of Islam is inward submission (al-inqiyad wa al-istislam), not outward shows. The proof is that God rebukes the Bedouins for claiming submission when they are not truthful, and He makes them Muslims only if they are guided to iman, i.e., inward faith. Therefore iman and Islam are one and the same.

Key Terms
دين
تبديل
اعتقاد
أفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that performing good deeds makes one a Muslim, and that deeds are part of the definition of Islam.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if deeds were part of the definition, everyone would constantly be changing religion, which is absurd.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the hadith about changing religion?
A) That changing religion is only about changing one's beliefs
B) That deeds are part of the religion
C) That religion is outward actions
D) That only hypocrites change religion

Key Takeaway
The hadith on changing religion proves that Islam is purely inward belief, as including deeds would lead to the absurdity of constant religious change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your Islam, do you measure it by your outward acts (prayer, charity) or by your innermost convictions? This lesson forces you to ask: what would be left of your Islam if your deeds fluctuated but your belief remained? Would you still consider yourself a Muslim?
?
Have you ever felt spiritually insecure because your worship habits changed? According to this argument, such insecurity is based on a false premise. What would it mean for your daily peace to anchor your identity solely in your belief in God and His Messenger, not in your performance?
?
Maturidi's reductio exposes the absurdity of judging someone's Islam by their deeds alone. Is there someone you have dismissed as 'not a real Muslim' because of their outward shortcomings? This lesson demands you examine your heart: do you truly accept that their belief, even if weak, makes them a Muslim?

Faith and Disbelief

Refuting the Objection: Outward Acts and the Quranic Proof from Surah al-Hujurat
Maturidi refutes the objection from outward acts using the Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the objection that Islam is mere outward acts by using the Quranic verse 'Say: We have submitted' and concludes that Islam is inward submission identical to iman.

Core Idea
Inward submission (al-inqiyad) is the reality of Islam, not outward shows.

A potential objection arises: the Prophet himself explained Islam in terms of outward acts (like the Five Pillars). And hypocrites also perform these acts. Maturidi addresses this by analyzing the verse from Surah al-Hujurat where God rebukes the Bedouins for claiming submission without true faith. He shows that true Islam is inward surrender, not just outward performance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection about outward acts
The opponent might cite hadith where Islam is defined by outward pillars, and note that hypocrites do them too.
This objection tries to prove that Islam is just outward actions.
2
Examine the 'Aslamna' verse
The verse 'Say: We have submitted' is questioned: is this submission true Islam? If yes, then sincere believers would be condemned as seekers of other religions.
This leads to an absurdity, so outward submission cannot be true Islam.
3
See the Quranic rebuke as evidence
God rejects mere outward claims: 'Say: Do not count your Islam as a favor to me...' He made them Muslims only if they are guided to iman.
Thus true Islam is inward faith, identical to iman.

الناس في عهد رسول الله ثلاثة : مؤمن وكافر ومنافق ، لم يُعرف للمسلم درجة خارجة من هؤلاء ولا للمؤمن ، وفي التفريق ذلك ، وذلك خلاف ما عليه الأمر الأول من الخلق . على أن أهل الأديان جميعا فروا عن اسم الإسلام ، فلو أنه ما معناه وما الذي نفر عنه يكن الاسلام معروفا عند طباعهم معنى لذلك ، وبه وصف الرسل أنهم سموا . وإذا ثبت أنه معلوم عند الخلق ، فمن رام صرفه إلى معنى زائد في الدين أو إلى معنى زائد على الإيمان أو ناقص كان لا يجب أن ذهب إلى معنى ناقص عنه أن يجعل الإسلام دون الإيمان فيجب حقيقته والتدين بذلك الدين ، ثم لا يكون مؤمنا . وإن كان زائدا فيجب أن لا يقع النفار عن قدر ما يدعون إلى الإيمان وإن لم يوصف لهم أنه أسلم ، فإذ وجد ذلك ثبت أن معنى ذلك غير زائد على الآخر ولا له وجود دونه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من بدل دينه فاقتلوه ، ثم بين الله دينه فقال : فَمَنْ يَكْفُرْ بِالطَّاغُوتِ وَيُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ ، فيقال : أهو مسلم أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، فقد بدل إذا دين الله ، وإن قال : نعم ، صار مسلما يفعل الإيمان لا غير. على أن هذا الخبر في تبديل الدين ، وأنه معروف أنه الاعتقاد لا غير ، وأن المراد في ذلك راجع إلى الدين الذي هو الإسلام ، ثبت أنه معروف الحد والقدر يعرف مبدله ، ولو كانت الأفعال سوى الاعتقاد دينا كان كل واحد في كل أحواله مبدل الدين لوجود تلك الأفعال أفعال من القرب في كل وقت ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال له : الخبر الذي رويت في هذا الباب في تفسير الإسلام فيه ذكر الأمور الظاهرة ، وكذلك أهل النفاق يوافقون المؤمنين في الأمور الظاهرة ، وقد . نعم : قيل لهم : قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ، أهو الإسلام في الحقيقة أو لا ؟ فإن قال : الإسلام في الحقيقة صير قوله : إِنَّ الدِّينَ عِنْدَ اللهِ الإِسْلَامُ ، وقوله : وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامِ دِينًا هو الذي ذكر، Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument by Imam al-Maturidi proving that Islam and iman (faith) are identical in their essential reality, and that mere outward actions do not constitute true Islam. He begins by noting that people in the Prophet's time fell into only three categories: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite—there was no intermediate degree for the Muslim separate from the believer. He then observes that all religious communities originally recoiled from the name 'Islam', implying that its meaning is instinctively known. Whoever tries to add or subtract from that meaning faces a dilemma: if Islam is less than iman, then one could be a Muslim without being a believer, which contradicts the Prophet's classification; if it is more, then the aversion to it would not occur as it does. Thus the meanings are not distinct. Next, he cites the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' and the verse 'whoever disbelieves in taghut and believes in God'. If asked whether such a person is Muslim, saying no makes him a changer of God's religion, but saying yes implies he is a Muslim solely through iman. The second part addresses an objection: the hadith about Islam mentions outward acts, and hypocrites also perform them. But the verse 'Say: We have submitted' (from Surah al-Hujurat) is questioned: is that submission true Islam? If yes, then other verses like 'The religion with God is Islam' would condemn sincere believers for seeking another religion. This is absurd. The proof is that God rebukes the Bedouins for claiming submission when they are not truthful, and He makes them Muslims only if they are guided to iman, i.e., inward faith. Therefore iman and Islam are one and the same.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the real meaning of Islam based on the Quranic verse 'They regard it as a favor...'?
A) Outward actions
B) Inward submission (al-inqiyad)
C) Verbal profession alone
D) Following the Prophet's example

Key Takeaway
Islam is not outward acts but inward submission (al-inqiyad), and this is proven by God's rebuke of those who only claim it outwardly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered your own outward religious acts—prayer, fasting, charity—as mere habits rather than expressions of inward submission? What would it take for you to transform them into true surrender?
?
The Bedouins claimed submission but were rebuked for lacking truthfulness. In which areas of your life might you be claiming submission to Allah without truly surrendering your heart?
?
If Allah were to ask you today, 'If you are truthful?' regarding your Islam, would you be able to answer with certainty that your faith is more than just outward performance?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

The Oneness of Islam and Iman
Maturidi refutes those who distinguish Islam from Iman, proving their unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islam and Iman refer to the same reality, and that separating them leads to contradictions with the Quran.

Core Idea
Islam and Iman are two names for one reality, not separate categories.

This passage from Imam Maturidi tackles a critical theological question: are Islam and Iman the same or different? Some had argued that Islam is merely outward submission while Iman is inner faith. Maturidi refutes this by showing that the Quran treats them as one, and that separating them leads to absurd consequences. Let's read his argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's position
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi starts by presenting an objection: if Islam is only outward submission, then hypocrites who professed submission would be Muslims, but the Quran condemns them.
2
Follow the refutation
Trace Maturidi's reasoning: if outward submission alone were Islam, then sincere believers would have sought a different religion, which is absurd. Therefore, true Islam must be inner submission.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Pay attention to the verses Maturidi cites: 3:85, 3:86, 49:17, and 2:136. See how he uses each to show that Islam is what is in the heart, not just words.
4
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the names 'Islam' and 'Iman' refer to one reality. Whoever tries to separate them is inventing falsehood. Reflect on the implications for understanding faith.

نعم : قيل لهم : قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا ... أهو الإسلام في الحقيقة أو لا؟ فإن قال: الإسلام في الحقيقة صير قوله: إِنَّ الدِّينَ عِنْدَ اللهِ الإِسْلَامُ، وقوله: وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامِ دِينًا، هو الذي ذكر، فيجب أن يكون قوله: "وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الاسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ فِي الآخِرَةِ مِنَ الخَاسِرِينَ"، وقال: وكَيْفَ يُهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمًا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إِيمَانِهِم، هو ذلك الذي قال لهم: قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا، وما جاء به الخبر لوجود تلك الشهادة فى أهل النفاق وتلك الأفعال عنهم/ فكون المخلصون والمؤمنون قد ابتغوا غير الإسلام دينا، وتركوا ما رضى الله وأهل النفاق الذين جاءوا به، وذلك بعيد. فثبت أن ذلك الإسلام الانقياد والاستسلام، وأما حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة لا ما ذكر من الظواهر، دليل ذلك الأمر الذى ذكروا أن الله قال فى آخر السورة: يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُلْ لا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكَم، ولو كان الإسلام ما أظهروا كيف قال: إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ. ثم فيه أنه جعلهم مسلمين كما قالوا إن هدوا للإيمان لا بما أظهروا، ثبت أن الإيمان هو الإسلام. وكذلك قال: وَمَنْ يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الإِسْلامَ دِينًا فَلَنْ يُقبَلُ مِنْهُ، ثم بين ذلك الدين الذي هو الإسلام. كَيْفَ يَهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمًا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إِيْمَانِهِمْ غير ذلك لم يقبل دينا غير الإيمان الذي وصف، ثم جعلهم مبدلين دين الإسلام بالكفر بعد الإيمان ليعلموا أنهما واحد. مع ما كان فيها تقدم كفاية من قوله: قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ إلَيْنَا، إلى قوله: مُسْلِمُونَ. والأصل عندنا أن الأسماء إنما جعلت لمعرفة أهلها فما أريدوا بأمور جعلت لهم وعليهم وفيما وعدوا وأوعدوا، ثم لم يكن أحد يخير فيما جرى آية الذكر باسم الإيمان أو الإسلام ممن ينتحل دين الإسلام فى اقتضاء الذكر إياه من حيث الاسم، ثبت أن حقيقتها واحد، وأن من يروم التفريق بينها من بعيد يخترع، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وآله الطيبين الطاهرين
Yes: It was said to them: 'Say: We have submitted...' Is this Islam in reality or not? If he says: 'Islam in reality', then His statement: 'Indeed, the religion with Allah is Islam' (3:19) and His statement: 'And I have chosen for you Islam as religion' (5:3) is that which he mentioned. So His statement: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him, and he, in the Hereafter, will be among the losers' (3:85) must be that. And He said: 'How shall Allah guide a people who disbelieved after their belief' (3:86), that is the same as what He said to them: 'Say: We have submitted.' And the report came about the existence of that testimony among the hypocrites and those deeds from them. So the sincere ones and the believers would have sought a religion other than Islam, and abandoned what Allah is pleased with, and the hypocrites who brought that, and that is farfetched. So it is established that that Islam is submission and surrender, but its reality is the religion in reality, not what is mentioned of outward appearances. The evidence for that is the matter which they mentioned that Allah said at the end of the surah: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say: Do not consider your submission a favor to me... if you should be truthful' (49:17). And if Islam were what they manifested, how could He say: 'if you should be truthful'? Then in it He made them Muslims as they said, if they were guided to belief not by what they manifested. So it is established that belief is Islam. And likewise He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' Then He clarified that religion which is Islam. How shall Allah guide a people who disbelieved after their belief other than that He does not accept a religion other than the belief which He described? Then He made them exchangers of the religion of Islam for disbelief after belief, so that they might know that they are one. Along with what was in it sufficient precedent from His statement: 'Say: We believe in Allah and what has been revealed to us' (2:136) up to His statement: 'Muslims.' And the principle with us is that names are only made for the knowledge of their people. So they were intended by matters made for them and against them and regarding what they were promised and warned. Then no one could choose regarding what the mention (al-dhikr) has come by the name of belief or Islam among those who profess the religion of Islam in requiring the mention of it regarding the name. So it is established that their reality is one, and that whoever seeks to differentiate between them from afar invents (falsehood). And there is no power except through Allah Almighty. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his pure and virtuous family.
Source pages p. 999

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who distinguish between Islam (outward submission) and Iman (inner faith), arguing that they are one reality. Maturidi presents an opponent's objection: If Islam is only outward submission, then the hypocrites who said 'we submit' would be Muslims, yet the Quran condemns them. This would lead to the absurd conclusion that sincere believers have sought a religion other than Islam. Therefore, the outward submission alone cannot be the true Islam. Maturidi then provides evidence from Quran 49:17, where Allah rebukes the Bedouins for claiming submission as a favor, and says 'if you are truthful', implying that their submission was not genuine. The verse shows that true Islam is what is in the heart, not just words. Further, in Quran 2:136, the believers are commanded to say 'we believe' and then are called Muslims, indicating interchangeability. Maturidi concludes that the names Islam and Iman refer to the same reality; whoever tries to separate them is inventing falsehood. The passage ends with a doxology.

Key Terms
الإسلام (al-Islam)
الإيمان (al-Iman)
النفاق (al-nifaq)
الانقياد (al-inqiyad)
الاستسلام (al-istislam)
الذكر (al-dhikr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Islam is only outward submission, while Iman is true inner faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that Islam and Iman are the same reality; true Islam is inner submission, and outward acts are expressions of that inner state.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Quranic verse 'Say: Do not consider your submission a favor to me... if you should be truthful' (49:17) prove about Islam?
A) Islam is only outward speech.
B) True Islam is genuine submission accepted by Allah, not mere outward words.
C) The hypocrites are true Muslims.
D) Submission is irrelevant to faith.

Key Takeaway
Islam and Iman are two names for the same reality of sincere submission to Allah, and any attempt to separate them contradicts the Quran and leads to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Question 1: You have likely identified as a 'Muslim' all your life. But when was the last time you paused to ask yourself: Is my Islam merely an outward identity, or does it reflect a heart that has truly submitted to Allah? What would change if you took this reality seriously today?
?
Question 2: Maturidi proves that Islam and Iman are one. If your faith (iman) is weak, can your Islam be acceptable? How does this truth confront you about the state of your heart right now?
?
Question 3: The hypocrites said 'We have submitted' but their hearts were empty. What if the people closest to you saw your true inner state—would they still recognize you as a believer? What is one specific act of hypocrisy you need to repent from today?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The Unity of Iman and Islam
Maturidi argues that the names iman and islam refer to one reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the names 'iman' and 'islam' refer to a single reality, based on Qur'anic evidence and the principle of naming.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are one reality, not two distinct things.

This lesson examines a key passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid where he argues that the terms 'iman' (faith) and 'islam' (submission) are not separate entities but refer to the same essential reality. Maturidi uses Qur'anic verses and a logical principle about names to demonstrate that these two terms are applied to the same people, proving their unity. Understanding this concept helps prevent theological confusion about the relationship between faith and submission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice that Maturidi starts with a Qur'anic question.
2
Identify the Qur'anic evidence
Find the verses cited (3:86 and 2:136). Note how Maturidi uses them to show that the same people are called both believers and Muslims.
The verse 2:136 ends with 'Muslims'.
3
Understand the principle of names
Maturidi states that names exist to identify their holders. If the same people are called by both names, then the reality behind them must be one.
This is a key logical principle.
4
Trace the logical conclusion
Follow how Maturidi concludes that the reality (haqiqa) of iman and islam is one, and any attempt to separate them is an innovation.
The conclusion is explicit: 'ثبت أن حقيقتها واحد'.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters: it prevents dividing the religion into separate compartments and emphasizes the unity of submission and faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَيْفَ يَهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمًا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إِيْمَانِهِمْ ير ذلك لم يقبل دينا غير الإيمان الذي وصف ، ثم جعلهم ميدلين دين الإسلام بالكفر بعد الإيمان ليعلموا أنهما واحد . مع ما كان فيها تقدم كفاية من قوله : قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ إلَيْنَا ، ٣ إلى قوله : مُسْلِمُونَ ، والأصل عندنا أن الأسماء إنما جعلت لمعرفة أهلها فما أريدوا بأمور جعلت لهم وعليهم وفيما وعدوا وأوعدوا ، ثم لم يكن أحد يخير فيما جرى آية الذكر باسم الإيمان أو الإسلام ممن ينتحل دين الإسلام فى اقتضاء الذكر إياه من حيث الاسم ، ثبت أن حقيقتها واحد ، وأن من يروم التفريق بينها من بعيد يخترع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى ، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وآله الطيبين الطاهرين
How shall Allah guide a people who disbelieved after their belief? [3:86] ... that He did not accept any religion other than the belief which He described, then He made them [؟] the religion of Islam with disbelief after belief so that they would know that they are one. And with what was in it a sufficient prior [proof] from His saying: 'Say: We believe in Allah and what has been sent down to us' [2:136] up to His saying: 'Muslims'. And the principle with us is that names are only made to identify their holders; so they are intended by matters made for them and against them and with regard to what they are promised and warned. Then no one who professes the religion of Islam was given a choice, in what the verse (āya) of the remembrance requires, to be called by the name of iman or islam—by virtue of the name. So it is established that their reality (ḥaqīqa) is one, and that whoever seeks to distinguish between them from afar invents [something]. And there is no power except in Allah the Exalted, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his pure and virtuous family.
Source pages p. 1000

Commentary
This passage is an argument (istidlāl) establishing that the terms 'iman' (belief) and 'islam' (submission) refer to a single reality (ḥaqīqa wāḥida). The author begins by citing a Qur'anic verse (3:86) that speaks of disbelief after belief, and then notes that Allah does not accept any religion other than that belief. He then references another verse (2:136) where the people are commanded to affirm belief in Allah and what was revealed, and they are called 'Muslims'. The author states that the underlying principle (al-aṣl) with the Maturidi school is that names (asmā') are instituted to identify their referents. The referents of 'iman' and 'islam' are the same people—those who profess Islam—and in the Qur'anic discourse, no such person is ever given a choice to be designated exclusively by one name rather than the other; rather, the same individuals are called both believers and Muslims. From this, the author concludes that the essential reality (ḥaqīqa) of iman and islam is one and the same. Whoever attempts to separate them (tafrīq) is innovating (yakhṭari‘) without basis. The passage ends with the standard formula of humility and blessings upon the Prophet.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الإسلام
الحقيقة
الاسم
التفريق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman and islam are different in essence or that one can have iman without islam.
Correction: Maturidi argues they are the same reality; the Qur'an applies both names to the same people, so they cannot be separated.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of this passage regarding the names 'iman' and 'islam'?
A) They are completely different realities.
B) Their reality is one and the same.
C) Iman is superior to islam.
D) The names are meaningless.

Key Takeaway
In Maturidi's view, 'iman' and 'islam' are names for the same single reality, and any attempt to separate them is an innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat your 'iman' as separate from your 'islam'—for example, feeling that your inner faith is weak while you still perform outward acts? The teacher says they are one reality. How will you work to align your inner state with your outer submission starting today?
?
Is there any area of your life where you outwardly submit (perform Islamic actions) but inwardly you do not truly believe? This passage says that is impossible in reality. What needs to change in your heart so that your actions become an honest expression of your faith?
?
If iman and islam are one, then your deeds are not optional additions to your faith—they are part of its very reality. What deed have you been neglecting that you now realize is essential? What concrete step will you take this week to live out that unity?
